# crcglot generated code gallery

Every block below is the actual output of `crcglot` for the `crc32` algorithm under different language / implementation choices.  Reproduce any of them with the listed command.  Each file embeds a `_self_test()` that asserts against the reveng catalogue's canonical check value (`crc("123456789") == 0xCBF43926` for crc32).

Want a different algorithm?  Substitute the name (`crcglot list` for the full catalogue) and re-run the command.

All examples here use `crc32` (reflected; refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF, ISO 3309 / Ethernet / PKZIP).  Non-reflected algorithms (e.g. `crc32-bzip2`) emit structurally different inner loops; see the source generators for the four shapes.

Every block is collapsed by default.  Click a heading to expand.  The Quick links section is a flat TOC of every (language x variant) cell -- useful for jumping straight to a single example.

Past the variant gallery, a [Comment styles](#comment-styles) section shows the same algorithm rendered in every documentation style each language supports (`--comment`), so you can match the doc convention your codebase already uses.

This file is auto-generated by `scripts/regenerate_examples.py`.  Do not hand-edit; re-run the script instead.

<summary>

### C / C++ — bit-by-bit

</summary>

```bash
crcglot c crc32
```

**Header (`.h`)**

```c
/* crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
 * Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
 * check: crc32(data, len) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
 *
 * Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
 * number of times over successive chunks of the message:
 *
 *     uint32_t s = crc32_init();
 *     s = crc32_update(s, chunk, chunk_len);
 *     uint32_t crc = crc32_finalize(s);
 *
 * One-shot: crc32(data, len)
 * Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns 0 on success; run it once on your
 *           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
 *
 * Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
 * Reproduce with crcglot:
 *     version:   0.22.0
 *     algorithm: crc32
 *     target:    c
 *     variant:   bitwise
 *     comment:   plain
 *     symbol:    crc32
 *     naming:    snake
 */
#ifndef CRC32_H
#define CRC32_H

#include <stdint.h>
#include <stddef.h>

#ifdef __cplusplus
extern "C" {
#endif

/* Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
 *
 * Returns the starting uint32_t state.
 */
uint32_t crc32_init(void);

/* Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
 *
 * state: running uint32_t state (from init or a prior update).
 * data: pointer to the message bytes.
 * len: number of bytes available at data.
 *
 * Returns the updated uint32_t state (not yet finalized).
 *
 * Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
 */
uint32_t crc32_update(uint32_t state, const uint8_t *data, size_t len);

/* Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
 *
 * state: accumulated uint32_t state from update.
 *
 * Returns the finished CRC value.
 *
 * Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
 */
uint32_t crc32_finalize(uint32_t state);

/* One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
 *
 * data: pointer to the message bytes.
 * len: number of bytes available at data.
 *
 * Returns the finished CRC value.
 */
uint32_t crc32(const uint8_t *data, size_t len);

/* Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
 *
 * Returns 0 iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
 *
 * Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
 *
 * Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
 */
int crc32_self_test(void);

#ifndef CRCGLOT_NO_PROVENANCE
#ifndef CRCGLOT_PROVENANCE_T_DEFINED
#define CRCGLOT_PROVENANCE_T_DEFINED
typedef struct {
    const char *version;
    const char *algorithm;
    const char *target;
    const char *variant;
    const char *comment;
    const char *symbol;
    const char *naming;
} crcglot_provenance_t;
#endif
extern const crcglot_provenance_t crc32_provenance;
#endif

#ifdef __cplusplus
}
#endif

#endif /* CRC32_H */
```

**Source (`.c`)**

```c
/* crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
 * Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
 * check: crc32(data, len) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
 *
 * Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
 * number of times over successive chunks of the message:
 *
 *     uint32_t s = crc32_init();
 *     s = crc32_update(s, chunk, chunk_len);
 *     uint32_t crc = crc32_finalize(s);
 *
 * One-shot: crc32(data, len)
 * Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns 0 on success; run it once on your
 *           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
 *
 * Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
 * Reproduce with crcglot:
 *     version:   0.22.0
 *     algorithm: crc32
 *     target:    c
 *     variant:   bitwise
 *     comment:   plain
 *     symbol:    crc32
 *     naming:    snake
 */
#include "crc32.h"

uint32_t crc32_init(void) {
    return 0xFFFFFFFFU;
}

uint32_t crc32_update(uint32_t state, const uint8_t *data, size_t len) {
    uint32_t crc = state;
    for (size_t i = 0; i < len; i++) {
        crc ^= data[i];
        for (int j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            if ((crc & 1U) != 0U) {
                crc = (crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320U;
            } else {
                crc >>= 1;
            }
        }
    }
    return crc;
}

uint32_t crc32_finalize(uint32_t state) {
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFFU;
}

uint32_t crc32(const uint8_t *data, size_t len) {
    return crc32_finalize(crc32_update(crc32_init(), data, len));
}

int crc32_self_test(void) {
    static const uint8_t kCheckInput[] = "123456789";
    int failed = 0;
    if (crc32(kCheckInput, 0) != 0x00000000U) {
        failed = 1;
    }
    if (crc32(kCheckInput, 9) != 0xCBF43926U) {
        failed = 1;
    }
    {
        uint32_t s = crc32_init();
        for (unsigned int i = 0U; i < 256U; i++) {
            uint8_t b = (uint8_t)i;
            s = crc32_update(s, &b, 1);
        }
        if (crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73U) {
            failed = 1;
        }
    }
    {
        uint32_t s = crc32_init();
        for (unsigned int i = 0U; i < 1024U; i++) {
            uint8_t b = (uint8_t)(((i * 167U) + 13U) & 0xFFU);
            s = crc32_update(s, &b, 1);
        }
        if (crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DBU) {
            failed = 1;
        }
    }
    return (failed != 0) ? 1 : 0;
}

#ifndef CRCGLOT_NO_PROVENANCE
const crcglot_provenance_t crc32_provenance = {
    .version   = "0.22.0",
    .algorithm = "crc32",
    .target    = "c",
    .variant   = "bitwise",
    .comment   = "plain",
    .symbol    = "crc32",
    .naming    = "snake",
};
#endif
```

</details>

### C / C++ — table-driven

```c
 * Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
 * check: crc32(data, len) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
 *
 * Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
 * number of times over successive chunks of the message:
 *
 *     uint32_t s = crc32_init();
 *     s = crc32_update(s, chunk, chunk_len);
 *     uint32_t crc = crc32_finalize(s);
 *
 * One-shot: crc32(data, len)
 * Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns 0 on success; run it once on your
 *           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
 *
 * Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
```

```c
    0x88085AE6U, 0xFF0F6A70U, 0x66063BCAU, 0x11010B5CU, 0x8F659EFFU, 0xF862AE69U, 0x616BFFD3U, 0x166CCF45U,
    0xA00AE278U, 0xD70DD2EEU, 0x4E048354U, 0x3903B3C2U, 0xA7672661U, 0xD06016F7U, 0x4969474DU, 0x3E6E77DBU,
    0xAED16A4AU, 0xD9D65ADCU, 0x40DF0B66U, 0x37D83BF0U, 0xA9BCAE53U, 0xDEBB9EC5U, 0x47B2CF7FU, 0x30B5FFE9U,
    0xBDBDF21CU, 0xCABAC28AU, 0x53B39330U, 0x24B4A3A6U, 0xBAD03605U, 0xCDD70693U, 0x54DE5729U, 0x23D967BFU,
    0xB3667A2EU, 0xC4614AB8U, 0x5D681B02U, 0x2A6F2B94U, 0xB40BBE37U, 0xC30C8EA1U, 0x5A05DF1BU, 0x2D02EF8DU
};

uint32_t crc32_init(void) {
    return 0xFFFFFFFFU;
}

uint32_t crc32_update(uint32_t state, const uint8_t *data, size_t len) {
    uint32_t crc = state;
    for (size_t i = 0; i < len; i++) {
        crc = crcglot_table_crc32[(crc ^ data[i]) & 0xFFU] ^ (crc >> 8);
    }
    return crc;
}

uint32_t crc32_finalize(uint32_t state) {
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFFU;
}

uint32_t crc32(const uint8_t *data, size_t len) {
    return crc32_finalize(crc32_update(crc32_init(), data, len));
}

int crc32_self_test(void) {
    static const uint8_t kCheckInput[] = "123456789";
    int failed = 0;
    if (crc32(kCheckInput, 0) != 0x00000000U) {
        failed = 1;
    }
    if (crc32(kCheckInput, 9) != 0xCBF43926U) {
        failed = 1;
    }
    {
        uint32_t s = crc32_init();
        for (unsigned int i = 0U; i < 256U; i++) {
            uint8_t b = (uint8_t)i;
            s = crc32_update(s, &b, 1);
        }
        if (crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73U) {
            failed = 1;
        }
    }
    {
        uint32_t s = crc32_init();
        for (unsigned int i = 0U; i < 1024U; i++) {
            uint8_t b = (uint8_t)(((i * 167U) + 13U) & 0xFFU);
            s = crc32_update(s, &b, 1);
        }
        if (crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DBU) {
            failed = 1;
        }
    }
    return (failed != 0) ? 1 : 0;
}

#ifndef CRCGLOT_NO_PROVENANCE
const crcglot_provenance_t crc32_provenance = {
    .version   = "0.22.0",
    .algorithm = "crc32",
    .target    = "c",
    .variant   = "table",
    .comment   = "plain",
    .symbol    = "crc32",
    .naming    = "snake",
};
#endif
```

<a id="example-c-slice8"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### C / C++ — slice-by-8

</summary>

```bash
crcglot c crc32 --slice8
```

**Header (`.h`)**

```c
/* crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
 * Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
 * check: crc32(data, len) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
 *
 * Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
 * number of times over successive chunks of the message:
 *
 *     uint32_t s = crc32_init();
 *     s = crc32_update(s, chunk, chunk_len);
 *     uint32_t crc = crc32_finalize(s);
 *
 * One-shot: crc32(data, len)
 * Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns 0 on success; run it once on your
 *           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
 *
 * Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
 * Reproduce with crcglot:
 *     version:   0.22.0
 *     algorithm: crc32
 *     target:    c
 *     variant:   slice8
 *     comment:   plain
 *     symbol:    crc32
 *     naming:    snake
 */
#ifndef CRC32_H
#define CRC32_H

#include <stdint.h>
#include <stddef.h>

#ifdef __cplusplus
extern "C" {
#endif

/* Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
 *
 * Returns the starting uint32_t state.
 */
uint32_t crc32_init(void);

/* Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
 *
 * state: running uint32_t state (from init or a prior update).
 * data: pointer to the message bytes.
 * len: number of bytes available at data.
 *
 * Returns the updated uint32_t state (not yet finalized).
 *
 * Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
 */
uint32_t crc32_update(uint32_t state, const uint8_t *data, size_t len);

/* Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
 *
 * state: accumulated uint32_t state from update.
 *
 * Returns the finished CRC value.
 *
 * Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
 */
uint32_t crc32_finalize(uint32_t state);

/* One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
 *
 * data: pointer to the message bytes.
 * len: number of bytes available at data.
 *
 * Returns the finished CRC value.
 */
uint32_t crc32(const uint8_t *data, size_t len);

/* Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
 *
 * Returns 0 iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
 *
 * Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
 *
 * Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
 */
int crc32_self_test(void);

#ifndef CRCGLOT_NO_PROVENANCE
#ifndef CRCGLOT_PROVENANCE_T_DEFINED
#define CRCGLOT_PROVENANCE_T_DEFINED
typedef struct {
    const char *version;
    const char *algorithm;
    const char *target;
    const char *variant;
    const char *comment;
    const char *symbol;
    const char *naming;
} crcglot_provenance_t;
#endif
extern const crcglot_provenance_t crc32_provenance;
#endif

#ifdef __cplusplus
}
#endif

#endif /* CRC32_H */
```

**Source (`.c`)**

```c
/* crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
 * Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
 * check: crc32(data, len) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
 *
 * Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
 * number of times over successive chunks of the message:
 *
 *     uint32_t s = crc32_init();
 *     s = crc32_update(s, chunk, chunk_len);
 *     uint32_t crc = crc32_finalize(s);
 *
 * One-shot: crc32(data, len)
 * Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns 0 on success; run it once on your

 *     comment:   plain
 *     symbol:    crc32
 *     naming:    snake
 */

        0x2C8E0FFFU, 0xE0240F61U, 0x6EAB0882U, 0xA201081CU, 0xA8C40105U, 0x646E019BU, 0xEAE10678U, 0x264B06E6U
    }
};

uint32_t crc32_init(void) {
    return 0xFFFFFFFFU;
}

uint32_t crc32_update(uint32_t state, const uint8_t *data, size_t len) {
    uint32_t crc = state;
    while (len >= 8U) {
        uint32_t b03 = (uint32_t)data[0] | (uint32_t)data[1] << 8 | (uint32_t)data[2] << 16 | (uint32_t)data[3] << 24;
        uint32_t b47 = (uint32_t)data[4] | (uint32_t)data[5] << 8 | (uint32_t)data[6] << 16 | (uint32_t)data[7] << 24;
        uint32_t xored = crc ^ b03;
        crc = crcglot_slice_crc32[7][ xored        & 0xFFU] ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[6][(xored >>  8) & 0xFFU]
            ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[5][(xored >> 16) & 0xFFU] ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[4][(xored >> 24) & 0xFFU]
            ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[3][ b47          & 0xFFU] ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[2][(b47   >>  8) & 0xFFU]
            ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[1][(b47   >> 16) & 0xFFU] ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[0][(b47   >> 24) & 0xFFU];
        data += 8;
        len -= 8U;
    }
    while (len > 0U) {
        crc = crcglot_slice_crc32[0][(crc ^ *data) & 0xFFU] ^ (crc >> 8);
        data++;
        len--;
    }
    return crc;
}

uint32_t crc32_finalize(uint32_t state) {
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFFU;
}

uint32_t crc32(const uint8_t *data, size_t len) {
    return crc32_finalize(crc32_update(crc32_init(), data, len));
}

int crc32_self_test(void) {
    static const uint8_t kCheckInput[] = "123456789";
    int failed = 0;
    if (crc32(kCheckInput, 0) != 0x00000000U) {
        failed = 1;
    }
    if (crc32(kCheckInput, 9) != 0xCBF43926U) {
        failed = 1;
    }
    {
        uint32_t s = crc32_init();
        for (unsigned int i = 0U; i < 256U; i++) {
            uint8_t b = (uint8_t)i;
            s = crc32_update(s, &b, 1);
        }
        if (crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73U) {
            failed = 1;
        }
    }
    {
        uint32_t s = crc32_init();
        for (unsigned int i = 0U; i < 1024U; i++) {
            uint8_t b = (uint8_t)(((i * 167U) + 13U) & 0xFFU);
            s = crc32_update(s, &b, 1);
        }
        if (crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DBU) {
            failed = 1;
        }
    }
    return (failed != 0) ? 1 : 0;
}

#ifndef CRCGLOT_NO_PROVENANCE
const crcglot_provenance_t crc32_provenance = {
    .version   = "0.22.0",
    .algorithm = "crc32",
    .target    = "c",
    .variant   = "slice8",
    .comment   = "plain",
    .symbol    = "crc32",
    .naming    = "snake",
};
#endif
```

<a id="example-csharp-bitwise"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### C# — bit-by-bit

</summary>

```bash
crcglot csharp crc32
```

```csharp
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: Crc32.Crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     uint s = Crc32.Crc32Init();
//     s = Crc32.Crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
//     uint crc = Crc32.Crc32Finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: Crc32.Crc32(data)
// Verify:   Crc32.Crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    csharp
//     variant:   bitwise
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    pascal

using System;

public static class Crc32
{
    // Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
    //
    // Returns the starting uint state.
    public static uint Crc32Init() {
        return 0xFFFFFFFFu;
    }

    // Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
    //
    // state: running uint state (from init or a prior update).
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the updated uint state (not yet finalized).
    //
    // Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    public static uint Crc32Update(uint state, byte[] data) {
        uint crc = state;
        foreach (byte b in data) {
            crc ^= b;
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
                if ((crc & 0x00000001u) != 0)
                    crc = (uint)((crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320u);
                else
                    crc >>= 1;
            }
        }
        return crc;
    }

    // Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
    //
    // state: accumulated uint state from update.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    public static uint Crc32Finalize(uint state) {
        return (uint)(state ^ 0xFFFFFFFFu);
    }

    // One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
    //
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    public static uint Crc32(byte[] data) {
        return Crc32Finalize(Crc32Update(Crc32Init(), data));
    }

    // Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
    //
    // Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
    //
    // Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
    //
    // Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    public static bool Crc32SelfTest() {
        if (Crc32(new byte[0]) != 0x00000000u) return false;
        if (Crc32(new byte[] { 0x31, 0x32, 0x33, 0x34, 0x35, 0x36, 0x37, 0x38, 0x39 }) != 0xCBF43926u) return false;
        {
            uint s = Crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
                s = Crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte)i });
            }
            if (Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73u) return false;
        }
        {
            uint s = Crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
                s = Crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte)((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) });
            }
            if (Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DBu) return false;
        }
        return true;
    }
}
```

```csharp
        0x86D3D2D4u, 0xF1D4E242u, 0x68DDB3F8u, 0x1FDA836Eu, 0x81BE16CDu, 0xF6B9265Bu, 0x6FB077E1u, 0x18B74777u,
        0x88085AE6u, 0xFF0F6A70u, 0x66063BCAu, 0x11010B5Cu, 0x8F659EFFu, 0xF862AE69u, 0x616BFFD3u, 0x166CCF45u,
        0xA00AE278u, 0xD70DD2EEu, 0x4E048354u, 0x3903B3C2u, 0xA7672661u, 0xD06016F7u, 0x4969474Du, 0x3E6E77DBu,
        0xAED16A4Au, 0xD9D65ADCu, 0x40DF0B66u, 0x37D83BF0u, 0xA9BCAE53u, 0xDEBB9EC5u, 0x47B2CF7Fu, 0x30B5FFE9u,
        0xBDBDF21Cu, 0xCABAC28Au, 0x53B39330u, 0x24B4A3A6u, 0xBAD03605u, 0xCDD70693u, 0x54DE5729u, 0x23D967BFu,
        0xB3667A2Eu, 0xC4614AB8u, 0x5D681B02u, 0x2A6F2B94u, 0xB40BBE37u, 0xC30C8EA1u, 0x5A05DF1Bu, 0x2D02EF8Du,
    };

    // Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
    //
    // Returns the starting uint state.
    public static uint Crc32Init() {
        return 0xFFFFFFFFu;
    }

    // Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
    //
    // state: running uint state (from init or a prior update).
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the updated uint state (not yet finalized).
    //
    // Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    public static uint Crc32Update(uint state, byte[] data) {
        uint crc = state;
        foreach (byte b in data) {
            crc = (uint)(_crcTable[(byte)(crc ^ b)] ^ (crc >> 8));
        }
        return crc;
    }

    // Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
    //
    // state: accumulated uint state from update.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    public static uint Crc32Finalize(uint state) {
        return (uint)(state ^ 0xFFFFFFFFu);
    }

    // One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
    //
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    public static uint Crc32(byte[] data) {
        return Crc32Finalize(Crc32Update(Crc32Init(), data));
    }

    // Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
    //
    // Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
    //
    // Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
    //
    // Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    public static bool Crc32SelfTest() {
        if (Crc32(new byte[0]) != 0x00000000u) return false;
        if (Crc32(new byte[] { 0x31, 0x32, 0x33, 0x34, 0x35, 0x36, 0x37, 0x38, 0x39 }) != 0xCBF43926u) return false;
        {
            uint s = Crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
                s = Crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte)i });
            }
            if (Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73u) return false;
        }
        {
            uint s = Crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
                s = Crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte)((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) });
            }
            if (Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DBu) return false;
        }
        return true;
    }
}
```

</details>

<a id="example-csharp-slice8"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### C# — slice-by-8

</summary>

```bash
crcglot csharp crc32 --slice8
```

```csharp
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: Crc32.Crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     uint s = Crc32.Crc32Init();
//     s = Crc32.Crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
//     uint crc = Crc32.Crc32Finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: Crc32.Crc32(data)

            0xFF6B144Au, 0x33C114D4u, 0xBD4E1337u, 0x71E413A9u, 0x7B211AB0u, 0xB78B1A2Eu, 0x39041DCDu, 0xF5AE1D53u,
            0x2C8E0FFFu, 0xE0240F61u, 0x6EAB0882u, 0xA201081Cu, 0xA8C40105u, 0x646E019Bu, 0xEAE10678u, 0x264B06E6u,
        },
    };

    // Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
    //
    // Returns the starting uint state.
    public static uint Crc32Init() {
        return 0xFFFFFFFFu;
    }

    // Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
    //
    // state: running uint state (from init or a prior update).
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the updated uint state (not yet finalized).
    //
    // Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    public static uint Crc32Update(uint state, byte[] data) {
        uint crc = state;
        int i = 0;
        while (i + 8 <= data.Length) {
            uint b03 = (uint)data[i] | (uint)data[i + 1] << 8 | (uint)data[i + 2] << 16 | (uint)data[i + 3] << 24;
            uint b47 = (uint)data[i + 4] | (uint)data[i + 5] << 8 | (uint)data[i + 6] << 16 | (uint)data[i + 7] << 24;
            uint xored = crc ^ b03;
            crc = _crcSliceTables[7, (byte)xored] ^ _crcSliceTables[6, (byte)(xored >> 8)]
                ^ _crcSliceTables[5, (byte)(xored >> 16)] ^ _crcSliceTables[4, (byte)(xored >> 24)]
                ^ _crcSliceTables[3, (byte)b47] ^ _crcSliceTables[2, (byte)(b47 >> 8)]
                ^ _crcSliceTables[1, (byte)(b47 >> 16)] ^ _crcSliceTables[0, (byte)(b47 >> 24)];
            i += 8;
        }
        while (i < data.Length) {
            crc = _crcSliceTables[0, (byte)(crc ^ data[i])] ^ (crc >> 8);
            i++;
        }
        return crc;
    }

    // Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
    //
    // state: accumulated uint state from update.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    public static uint Crc32Finalize(uint state) {
        return (uint)(state ^ 0xFFFFFFFFu);
    }

    // One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
    //
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    public static uint Crc32(byte[] data) {
        return Crc32Finalize(Crc32Update(Crc32Init(), data));
    }

    // Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
    //
    // Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
    //
    // Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
    //
    // Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    public static bool Crc32SelfTest() {
        if (Crc32(new byte[0]) != 0x00000000u) return false;
        if (Crc32(new byte[] { 0x31, 0x32, 0x33, 0x34, 0x35, 0x36, 0x37, 0x38, 0x39 }) != 0xCBF43926u) return false;
        {
            uint s = Crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
                s = Crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte)i });
            }
            if (Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73u) return false;
        }
        {
            uint s = Crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
                s = Crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte)((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) });
            }
            if (Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DBu) return false;
        }
        return true;
    }
}
```

<a id="example-go-bitwise"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### Go — bit-by-bit

</summary>

```bash
crcglot go crc32
```

```go
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: Crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     s := Crc32Init()
//     s = Crc32Update(s, chunk)  // over each chunk of the message
//     crc := Crc32Finalize(s)
//
// One-shot: Crc32(data)
// Verify:   Crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    go
//     variant:   bitwise
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    pascal

package crc

// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
//
// Returns the starting uint32 state.
func Crc32Init() uint32 {
    return 0xFFFFFFFF
}

// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
//
// state: running uint32 state (from init or a prior update).
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the updated uint32 state (not yet finalized).
//
// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
func Crc32Update(state uint32, data []byte) uint32 {
    crc := state
    for _, b := range data {
        crc ^= uint32(b)
        for i := 0; i < 8; i++ {
            if crc&1 != 0 {
                crc = (crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320
            } else {
                crc >>= 1
            }
        }
    }
    return crc
}

// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
//
// state: accumulated uint32 state from update.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
//
// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
func Crc32Finalize(state uint32) uint32 {
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF
}

// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
//
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
func Crc32(data []byte) uint32 {
    return Crc32Finalize(Crc32Update(Crc32Init(), data))
}

// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
//
// Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
//
// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
//
// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
func Crc32SelfTest() bool {
    if Crc32([]byte("")) != 0x00000000 {
        return false
    }
    if Crc32([]byte("123456789")) != 0xCBF43926 {
        return false
    }
    s := Crc32Init()
    for i := 0; i < 256; i++ {
        s = Crc32Update(s, []byte{byte(i)})
    }
    if Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73 {
        return false
    }
    s = Crc32Init()
    for i := 0; i < 1024; i++ {
        s = Crc32Update(s, []byte{byte((i*167 + 13) & 0xFF)})
    }
    if Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB {
        return false
    }
    return true
}
```

</details>

```go
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any

    0xAED16A4A, 0xD9D65ADC, 0x40DF0B66, 0x37D83BF0, 0xA9BCAE53, 0xDEBB9EC5, 0x47B2CF7F, 0x30B5FFE9,
    0xBDBDF21C, 0xCABAC28A, 0x53B39330, 0x24B4A3A6, 0xBAD03605, 0xCDD70693, 0x54DE5729, 0x23D967BF,
    0xB3667A2E, 0xC4614AB8, 0x5D681B02, 0x2A6F2B94, 0xB40BBE37, 0xC30C8EA1, 0x5A05DF1B, 0x2D02EF8D,
}

// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
//
// Returns the starting uint32 state.
func Crc32Init() uint32 {
    return 0xFFFFFFFF
}

// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
//
// state: running uint32 state (from init or a prior update).
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the updated uint32 state (not yet finalized).
//
// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
func Crc32Update(state uint32, data []byte) uint32 {
    crc := state
    for _, b := range data {
        crc = _crc32_table[uint32(byte(crc)^b)] ^ (crc >> 8)
    }
    return crc
}

// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
//
// state: accumulated uint32 state from update.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
//
// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
func Crc32Finalize(state uint32) uint32 {
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF
}

// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
//
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
func Crc32(data []byte) uint32 {
    return Crc32Finalize(Crc32Update(Crc32Init(), data))
}

// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
//
// Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
//
// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
//
// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
func Crc32SelfTest() bool {
    if Crc32([]byte("")) != 0x00000000 {
        return false
    }
    if Crc32([]byte("123456789")) != 0xCBF43926 {
        return false
    }
    s := Crc32Init()
    for i := 0; i < 256; i++ {
        s = Crc32Update(s, []byte{byte(i)})
    }
    if Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73 {
        return false
    }
    s = Crc32Init()
    for i := 0; i < 1024; i++ {
        s = Crc32Update(s, []byte{byte((i*167 + 13) & 0xFF)})
    }
    if Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB {
        return false
    }
    return true
}
```

</details>

<a id="example-go-slice8"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### Go — slice-by-8

</summary>

```bash
crcglot go crc32 --slice8
```

```go
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: Crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     s := Crc32Init()
//     s = Crc32Update(s, chunk)  // over each chunk of the message
//     crc := Crc32Finalize(s)
//
// One-shot: Crc32(data)
// Verify:   Crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your

        0xFF6B144A, 0x33C114D4, 0xBD4E1337, 0x71E413A9, 0x7B211AB0, 0xB78B1A2E, 0x39041DCD, 0xF5AE1D53,
        0x2C8E0FFF, 0xE0240F61, 0x6EAB0882, 0xA201081C, 0xA8C40105, 0x646E019B, 0xEAE10678, 0x264B06E6,

}

// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
//
// Returns the starting uint32 state.
func Crc32Init() uint32 {
    return 0xFFFFFFFF
}

// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
//
// state: running uint32 state (from init or a prior update).
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the updated uint32 state (not yet finalized).
//
// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
func Crc32Update(state uint32, data []byte) uint32 {
    crc := state
    for len(data) >= 8 {
        b03 := uint32(data[0]) | uint32(data[1])<<8 | uint32(data[2])<<16 | uint32(data[3])<<24
        b47 := uint32(data[4]) | uint32(data[5])<<8 | uint32(data[6])<<16 | uint32(data[7])<<24
        xored := crc ^ b03
        crc = _crc32_sliceTables[7][byte(xored)] ^ _crc32_sliceTables[6][byte(xored>>8)] ^
            _crc32_sliceTables[5][byte(xored>>16)] ^ _crc32_sliceTables[4][byte(xored>>24)] ^
            _crc32_sliceTables[3][byte(b47)] ^ _crc32_sliceTables[2][byte(b47>>8)] ^
            _crc32_sliceTables[1][byte(b47>>16)] ^ _crc32_sliceTables[0][byte(b47>>24)]
        data = data[8:]
    }
    for _, b := range data {
        crc = _crc32_sliceTables[0][byte(crc)^b] ^ (crc >> 8)
    }
    return crc
}

// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
//
// state: accumulated uint32 state from update.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
//
// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
func Crc32Finalize(state uint32) uint32 {
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF
}

// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
//
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
func Crc32(data []byte) uint32 {
    return Crc32Finalize(Crc32Update(Crc32Init(), data))
}

// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
//
// Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
//
// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
//
// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
func Crc32SelfTest() bool {
    if Crc32([]byte("")) != 0x00000000 {
        return false
    }
    if Crc32([]byte("123456789")) != 0xCBF43926 {
        return false
    }
    s := Crc32Init()
    for i := 0; i < 256; i++ {
        s = Crc32Update(s, []byte{byte(i)})
    }
    if Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73 {
        return false
    }
    s = Crc32Init()
    for i := 0; i < 1024; i++ {
        s = Crc32Update(s, []byte{byte((i*167 + 13) & 0xFF)})
    }
    if Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB {
        return false
    }
    return true
}
```

</details>

<a id="example-java-bitwise"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### Java — bit-by-bit

</summary>

```bash
crcglot java crc32
```

```java
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: CrcGlot.crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     int s = CrcGlot.crc32Init();
//     s = CrcGlot.crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
//     int crc = CrcGlot.crc32Finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: CrcGlot.crc32(data)
// Verify:   CrcGlot.crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    java
//     variant:   bitwise
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    camel

public final class CrcGlot {
    // Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
    //
    // Returns the starting int state.
    public static int crc32Init() {
        return 0xFFFFFFFF;
    }

    // Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
    //
    // state: running int state (from init or a prior update).
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the updated int state (not yet finalized).
    //
    // Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    public static int crc32Update(int state, byte[] data) {
        int crc = state;
        for (byte b : data) {
            crc ^= (b & 0xFF);
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
                if ((crc & 1) != 0)
                    crc = (crc >>> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320;
                else
                    crc >>>= 1;
            }
        }
        return crc;
    }

    // Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
    //
    // state: accumulated int state from update.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    //
    // width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
    public static int crc32Finalize(int state) {
        return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF;
    }

    // One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
    //
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
    public static int crc32(byte[] data) {
        return crc32Finalize(crc32Update(crc32Init(), data));
    }

    // Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
    //
    // Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
    //
    // Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
    //
    // Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    public static boolean crc32SelfTest() {
        if (crc32(new byte[0]) != 0x00000000) return false;
        if (crc32(new byte[] { 0x31, 0x32, 0x33, 0x34, 0x35, 0x36, 0x37, 0x38, 0x39 }) != 0xCBF43926) return false;
        {
            int s = crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
                s = crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte) i });
            }
            if (crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73) return false;
        }
        {
            int s = crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
                s = crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte) ((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) });
            }
            if (crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB) return false;
        }
        return true;
    }
}
```

</details>

```bash
crcglot java crc32 --table
```

```java
    // Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
    //
    // Returns the starting int state.
    public static int crc32Init() {
        return 0xFFFFFFFF;
    }

    // Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
    //
    // state: running int state (from init or a prior update).
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the updated int state (not yet finalized).
    //
    // Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    public static int crc32Update(int state, byte[] data) {
        int crc = state;
        for (byte b : data) {
            crc = crcglot_table_crc32[((crc ^ (b & 0xFF)) & 0xFF)] ^ (crc >>> 8);
        }
        return crc;
    }

    // Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
    //
    // state: accumulated int state from update.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    //
    // width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
    public static int crc32Finalize(int state) {
        return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF;
    }

    // One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
    //
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
    public static int crc32(byte[] data) {
        return crc32Finalize(crc32Update(crc32Init(), data));
    }

    // Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
    //
    // Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
    //
    // Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
    //
    // Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    public static boolean crc32SelfTest() {
        if (crc32(new byte[0]) != 0x00000000) return false;
        if (crc32(new byte[] { 0x31, 0x32, 0x33, 0x34, 0x35, 0x36, 0x37, 0x38, 0x39 }) != 0xCBF43926) return false;
        {
            int s = crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
                s = crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte) i });
            }
            if (crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73) return false;
        }
        {
            int s = crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
                s = crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte) ((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) });
            }
            if (crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB) return false;
        }
        return true;
    }
}
```

</details>

<a id="example-java-slice8"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### Java — slice-by-8

</summary>

```bash
crcglot java crc32 --slice8
```

```java
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: CrcGlot.crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     int s = CrcGlot.crc32Init();
//     s = CrcGlot.crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
//     int crc = CrcGlot.crc32Finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: CrcGlot.crc32(data)

            0x061D761C, 0xCAB77682, 0x44387161, 0x889271FF, 0x825778E6, 0x4EFD7878, 0xC0727F9B, 0x0CD87F05,
            0xD5F86DA9, 0x19526D37, 0x97DD6AD4, 0x5B776A4A, 0x51B26353, 0x9D1863CD, 0x1397642E, 0xDF3D64B0,
            0x83D02561, 0x4F7A25FF, 0xC1F5221C, 0x0D5F2282, 0x079A2B9B, 0xCB302B05, 0x45BF2CE6, 0x89152C78,
            0x50353ED4, 0x9C9F3E4A, 0x121039A9, 0xDEBA3937, 0xD47F302E, 0x18D530B0, 0x965A3753, 0x5AF037CD,
            0xFF6B144A, 0x33C114D4, 0xBD4E1337, 0x71E413A9, 0x7B211AB0, 0xB78B1A2E, 0x39041DCD, 0xF5AE1D53,
            0x2C8E0FFF, 0xE0240F61, 0x6EAB0882, 0xA201081C, 0xA8C40105, 0x646E019B, 0xEAE10678, 0x264B06E6,
        },
    };

    // Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
    //
    // Returns the starting int state.
    public static int crc32Init() {
        return 0xFFFFFFFF;
    }

    // Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
    //
    // state: running int state (from init or a prior update).
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the updated int state (not yet finalized).
    //
    // Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    public static int crc32Update(int state, byte[] data) {
        int crc = state;
        int i = 0;
        while (i + 8 <= data.length) {
            int b03 = (data[i] & 0xFF) | ((data[i + 1] & 0xFF) << 8) | ((data[i + 2] & 0xFF) << 16) | ((data[i + 3] & 0xFF) << 24);
            int b47 = (data[i + 4] & 0xFF) | ((data[i + 5] & 0xFF) << 8) | ((data[i + 6] & 0xFF) << 16) | ((data[i + 7] & 0xFF) << 24);
            int xored = crc ^ b03;
            crc = crcglot_slice_crc32[7][xored & 0xFF] ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[6][(xored >>> 8) & 0xFF]
                ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[5][(xored >>> 16) & 0xFF] ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[4][(xored >>> 24) & 0xFF]
                ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[3][b47 & 0xFF] ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[2][(b47 >>> 8) & 0xFF]
                ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[1][(b47 >>> 16) & 0xFF] ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[0][(b47 >>> 24) & 0xFF];
            i += 8;
        }
        while (i < data.length) {
            crc = crcglot_slice_crc32[0][(crc ^ (data[i] & 0xFF)) & 0xFF] ^ (crc >>> 8);
            i++;
        }
        return crc;
    }

    // Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
    //
    // state: accumulated int state from update.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    //
    // width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
    public static int crc32Finalize(int state) {
        return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF;
    }

    // One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
    //
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
    public static int crc32(byte[] data) {
        return crc32Finalize(crc32Update(crc32Init(), data));
    }

    // Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
    //
    // Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
    //
    // Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
    //
    // Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    public static boolean crc32SelfTest() {
        if (crc32(new byte[0]) != 0x00000000) return false;
        if (crc32(new byte[] { 0x31, 0x32, 0x33, 0x34, 0x35, 0x36, 0x37, 0x38, 0x39 }) != 0xCBF43926) return false;
        {
            int s = crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
                s = crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte) i });
            }
            if (crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73) return false;
        }
        {
            int s = crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
                s = crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte) ((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) });
            }
            if (crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB) return false;
        }
        return true;
    }
}
```

</details>

<a id="example-python-bitwise"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### Python — bit-by-bit

</summary>

```bash
crcglot python crc32
```

```python
"""crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926

Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
number of times over successive chunks of the message:

    s = crc32_init()
    s = crc32_update(s, chunk)  # over each chunk of the message
    crc = crc32_finalize(s)

One-shot: crc32(data)
Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns True on success; run it once on your
          toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.

Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
Reproduce with crcglot:
    version:   0.22.0
    algorithm: crc32
    target:    python
    variant:   bitwise
    comment:   plain
    symbol:    crc32
    naming:    snake
"""


def crc32_init() -> int:
    """Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.

    Returns the starting int state.
    """
    return 0xFFFFFFFF


def crc32_update(state: int, data: bytes) -> int:
    """Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.

    state: running int state (from init or a prior update).
    data: the message bytes (a bytes-like object).

    Returns the updated int state (not yet finalized).

    Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    """
    crc = state
    for byte in data:
        crc ^= byte
        for _ in range(8):
            if crc & 1:
                crc = (crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320
            else:
                crc >>= 1
    return crc


def crc32_finalize(state: int) -> int:
    """Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.

    state: accumulated int state from update.

    Returns the finished CRC value.

    Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    """
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF


def crc32(data: bytes) -> int:
    """One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.

    data: the message bytes (a bytes-like object).

    Returns the finished CRC value.
    """
    state = crc32_init()
    state = crc32_update(state, data)
    return crc32_finalize(state)


def crc32_self_test() -> bool:
    """Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.

    Returns True iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.

    Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.

    Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    """
    if crc32(b"") != 0x00000000:
        return False
    if crc32(b"123456789") != 0xCBF43926:
        return False
    s = crc32_init()
    for i in range(256):
        s = crc32_update(s, bytes([i]))
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73:
        return False
    s = crc32_init()
    for i in range(1024):
        s = crc32_update(s, bytes([(i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF]))
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB:
        return False
    return True
```

```python
    0xAED16A4A, 0xD9D65ADC, 0x40DF0B66, 0x37D83BF0, 0xA9BCAE53, 0xDEBB9EC5, 0x47B2CF7F, 0x30B5FFE9,
    0xBDBDF21C, 0xCABAC28A, 0x53B39330, 0x24B4A3A6, 0xBAD03605, 0xCDD70693, 0x54DE5729, 0x23D967BF,
    0xB3667A2E, 0xC4614AB8, 0x5D681B02, 0x2A6F2B94, 0xB40BBE37, 0xC30C8EA1, 0x5A05DF1B, 0x2D02EF8D,
)
# fmt: on


def crc32_init() -> int:
    """Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.

    Returns the starting int state.
    """
    return 0xFFFFFFFF


def crc32_update(state: int, data: bytes) -> int:
    """Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.

    state: running int state (from init or a prior update).
    data: the message bytes (a bytes-like object).

    Returns the updated int state (not yet finalized).

    Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    """
    crc = state
    for byte in data:
        crc = _crcglot_table_crc32[(crc ^ byte) & 0xFF] ^ (crc >> 8)
    return crc


def crc32_finalize(state: int) -> int:
    """Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.

    state: accumulated int state from update.

    Returns the finished CRC value.

    Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    """
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF


def crc32(data: bytes) -> int:
    """One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.

    data: the message bytes (a bytes-like object).

    Returns the finished CRC value.
    """
    state = crc32_init()
    state = crc32_update(state, data)
    return crc32_finalize(state)


def crc32_self_test() -> bool:
    """Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.

    Returns True iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.

    Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.

    Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    """
    if crc32(b"") != 0x00000000:
        return False
    if crc32(b"123456789") != 0xCBF43926:
        return False
    s = crc32_init()
    for i in range(256):
        s = crc32_update(s, bytes([i]))
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73:
        return False
    s = crc32_init()
    for i in range(1024):
        s = crc32_update(s, bytes([(i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF]))
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB:
        return False
    return True
```

<summary>

### Rust — bit-by-bit

</summary>

```bash
crcglot rust crc32
```

```rust
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     let s = crc32_init();
//     let s = crc32_update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
//     let crc = crc32_finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: crc32(data)
// Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    rust
//     variant:   bitwise
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    snake

/// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
///
/// Returns the starting u32 state.
pub fn crc32_init() -> u32 {
    0xFFFFFFFF
}

/// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
///
/// state: running u32 state (from init or a prior update).
/// data: the message bytes.
///
/// Returns the updated u32 state (not yet finalized).
///
/// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
pub fn crc32_update(state: u32, data: &[u8]) -> u32 {
    let mut crc: u32 = state;
    for &byte in data {
        crc ^= byte as u32;
        for _ in 0..8 {
            if crc & 1 != 0 {
                crc = (crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320;
            } else {
                crc >>= 1;
            }
        }
    }
    crc
}

/// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
///
/// state: accumulated u32 state from update.
///
/// Returns the finished CRC value.
///
/// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
pub fn crc32_finalize(state: u32) -> u32 {
    state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF
}

/// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
///
/// data: the message bytes.
///
/// Returns the finished CRC value.
pub fn crc32(data: &[u8]) -> u32 {
    crc32_finalize(crc32_update(crc32_init(), data))
}

/// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
///
/// Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
///
/// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
///
/// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
pub fn crc32_self_test() -> bool {
    if crc32(b"") != 0x00000000_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    if crc32(b"123456789") != 0xCBF43926_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    let mut s = crc32_init();
    for i in 0u32..256 {
        s = crc32_update(s, &[i as u8]);
    }
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    s = crc32_init();
    for i in 0u32..1024 {
        s = crc32_update(s, &[((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) as u8]);
    }
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    true
}
```

</details>

```rust
    0xB3667A2E, 0xC4614AB8, 0x5D681B02, 0x2A6F2B94, 0xB40BBE37, 0xC30C8EA1, 0x5A05DF1B, 0x2D02EF8D,

// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     let s = crc32_init();
//     let s = crc32_update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
//     let crc = crc32_finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: crc32(data)
// Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    rust
//     variant:   table
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    snake

/// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
///
/// Returns the starting u32 state.
pub fn crc32_init() -> u32 {
    0xFFFFFFFF
}

/// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
///
/// state: running u32 state (from init or a prior update).
/// data: the message bytes.
///
/// Returns the updated u32 state (not yet finalized).
///
/// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
pub fn crc32_update(state: u32, data: &[u8]) -> u32 {
    let mut crc: u32 = state;
    for &byte in data {
        crc = CRCGLOT_TABLE_CRC32[(crc ^ byte as u32) as usize & 0xFF] ^ (crc >> 8);
    }
    crc
}

/// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
///
/// state: accumulated u32 state from update.
///
/// Returns the finished CRC value.
///
/// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
pub fn crc32_finalize(state: u32) -> u32 {
    state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF
}

/// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
///
/// data: the message bytes.
///
/// Returns the finished CRC value.
pub fn crc32(data: &[u8]) -> u32 {
    crc32_finalize(crc32_update(crc32_init(), data))
}

/// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
///
/// Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
///
/// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
///
/// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
pub fn crc32_self_test() -> bool {
    if crc32(b"") != 0x00000000_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    if crc32(b"123456789") != 0xCBF43926_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    let mut s = crc32_init();
    for i in 0u32..256 {
        s = crc32_update(s, &[i as u8]);
    }
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    s = crc32_init();
    for i in 0u32..1024 {
        s = crc32_update(s, &[((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) as u8]);
    }
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    true
}
```

```rust
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     let s = crc32_init();
//     let s = crc32_update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
//     let crc = crc32_finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: crc32(data)
// Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Variant: slice-by-8 (8 tables, ~10x throughput vs a plain table for large buffers).
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    rust
//     variant:   slice8
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    snake

/// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
///
/// Returns the starting u32 state.
pub fn crc32_init() -> u32 {
    0xFFFFFFFF
}

/// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
///
/// state: running u32 state (from init or a prior update).
/// data: the message bytes.
///
/// Returns the updated u32 state (not yet finalized).
///
/// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
pub fn crc32_update(state: u32, data: &[u8]) -> u32 {
    let mut crc: u32 = state;
    let n = data.len();
    let mut i: usize = 0;
    while i + 8 <= n {
        let b03 = data[i] as u32 | (data[i+1] as u32) << 8 | (data[i+2] as u32) << 16 | (data[i+3] as u32) << 24;
        let b47 = data[i+4] as u32 | (data[i+5] as u32) << 8 | (data[i+6] as u32) << 16 | (data[i+7] as u32) << 24;
        let xored = crc ^ b03;
        crc = CRCGLOT_SLICE_CRC32[7][ (xored        & 0xFF) as usize] ^ CRCGLOT_SLICE_CRC32[6][((xored >>  8) & 0xFF) as usize]
            ^ CRCGLOT_SLICE_CRC32[5][((xored >> 16) & 0xFF) as usize] ^ CRCGLOT_SLICE_CRC32[4][((xored >> 24) & 0xFF) as usize]
            ^ CRCGLOT_SLICE_CRC32[3][ (b47          & 0xFF) as usize] ^ CRCGLOT_SLICE_CRC32[2][((b47   >>  8) & 0xFF) as usize]
            ^ CRCGLOT_SLICE_CRC32[1][((b47   >> 16) & 0xFF) as usize] ^ CRCGLOT_SLICE_CRC32[0][((b47   >> 24) & 0xFF) as usize];
        i += 8;
    }
    while i < n {
        crc = CRCGLOT_SLICE_CRC32[0][((crc ^ data[i] as u32) & 0xFF) as usize] ^ (crc >> 8);
        i += 1;
    }
    crc
}

/// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
///
/// state: accumulated u32 state from update.
///
/// Returns the finished CRC value.
///
/// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
pub fn crc32_finalize(state: u32) -> u32 {
    state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF
}

/// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
///
/// data: the message bytes.
///
/// Returns the finished CRC value.
pub fn crc32(data: &[u8]) -> u32 {
    crc32_finalize(crc32_update(crc32_init(), data))
}

/// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
///
/// Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
///
/// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
///
/// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
pub fn crc32_self_test() -> bool {
    if crc32(b"") != 0x00000000_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    if crc32(b"123456789") != 0xCBF43926_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    let mut s = crc32_init();
    for i in 0u32..256 {
        s = crc32_update(s, &[i as u8]);
    }
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    s = crc32_init();
    for i in 0u32..1024 {
        s = crc32_update(s, &[((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) as u8]);
    }
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    true
}
```

<a id="example-typescript-bitwise"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### TypeScript — bit-by-bit

</summary>

```bash
crcglot typescript crc32
```

```typescript
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     let s = crc32Init();
//     s = crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk of the message
//     const crc = crc32Finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: crc32(data)
// Verify:   crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    typescript
//     variant:   bitwise
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    camel

// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
//
// Returns the starting number state.
export function crc32Init(): number {
    return 0xFFFFFFFF;
}

// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
//
// state: running number state (from init or a prior update).
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the updated number state (not yet finalized).
//
// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
export function crc32Update(state: number, data: Uint8Array): number {
    let crc: number = state;
    for (const byte of data) {
        crc ^= byte;
        for (let j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            if ((crc & 1) !== 0) {
                crc = (crc >>> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320;
            } else {
                crc >>>= 1;
            }
        }
    }
    return crc;
}

// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
//
// state: accumulated number state from update.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
//
// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
export function crc32Finalize(state: number): number {
    return (state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF) >>> 0;
}

// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
//
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
export function crc32(data: Uint8Array): number {
    return crc32Finalize(crc32Update(crc32Init(), data));
}

// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
//
// Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
//
// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
//
// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
export function crc32SelfTest(): boolean {
    if (crc32(new Uint8Array([])) !== 0x00000000) return false;
    if (crc32(new Uint8Array([0x31,0x32,0x33,0x34,0x35,0x36,0x37,0x38,0x39])) !== 0xCBF43926) return false;
    {
        let s = crc32Init();
        for (let i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
            s = crc32Update(s, new Uint8Array([i]));
        }
        if (crc32Finalize(s) !== 0x29058C73) return false;
    }
    {
        let s = crc32Init();
        for (let i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
            s = crc32Update(s, new Uint8Array([(i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF]));
        }
        if (crc32Finalize(s) !== 0x6D4552DB) return false;
    }
    return true;
}
```

</details>

```typescript
const crcglot_table_crc32: number[] = [
    0x00000000, 0x77073096, 0xEE0E612C, 0x990951BA, 0x076DC419, 0x706AF48F, 0xE963A535, 0x9E6495A3,
    0x0EDB8832, 0x79DCB8A4, 0xE0D5E91E, 0x97D2D988, 0x09B64C2B, 0x7EB17CBD, 0xE7B82D07, 0x90BF1D91,

// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     let s = crc32Init();
//     s = crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk of the message
//     const crc = crc32Finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: crc32(data)
// Verify:   crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    typescript
//     variant:   table
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    camel

// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
//
// Returns the starting number state.
export function crc32Init(): number {
    return 0xFFFFFFFF;
}

// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
//
// state: running number state (from init or a prior update).
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the updated number state (not yet finalized).
//
// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
export function crc32Update(state: number, data: Uint8Array): number {
    let crc: number = state;
    for (const byte of data) {
        crc = crcglot_table_crc32[(crc ^ byte) & 0xFF] ^ (crc >>> 8);
    }
    return crc;
}

// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
//
// state: accumulated number state from update.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
//
// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
export function crc32Finalize(state: number): number {
    return (state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF) >>> 0;
}

// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
//
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
export function crc32(data: Uint8Array): number {
    return crc32Finalize(crc32Update(crc32Init(), data));
}

// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
//
// Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
//
// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
//
// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
export function crc32SelfTest(): boolean {
    if (crc32(new Uint8Array([])) !== 0x00000000) return false;
    if (crc32(new Uint8Array([0x31,0x32,0x33,0x34,0x35,0x36,0x37,0x38,0x39])) !== 0xCBF43926) return false;
    {
        let s = crc32Init();
        for (let i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
            s = crc32Update(s, new Uint8Array([i]));
        }
        if (crc32Finalize(s) !== 0x29058C73) return false;
    }
    {
        let s = crc32Init();
        for (let i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
            s = crc32Update(s, new Uint8Array([(i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF]));
        }
        if (crc32Finalize(s) !== 0x6D4552DB) return false;
    }
    return true;
}
```

```typescript
        0x50353ED4, 0x9C9F3E4A, 0x121039A9, 0xDEBA3937, 0xD47F302E, 0x18D530B0, 0x965A3753, 0x5AF037CD,
        0xFF6B144A, 0x33C114D4, 0xBD4E1337, 0x71E413A9, 0x7B211AB0, 0xB78B1A2E, 0x39041DCD, 0xF5AE1D53,
```
