```typescript
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     let s = crc32Init();
//     s = crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk of the message
//     const crc = crc32Finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: crc32(data)
// Verify:   crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Variant: slice-by-8 (8 tables, ~10x throughput vs a plain table for large buffers).
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    typescript
//     variant:   slice8
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    camel

// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
//
// Returns the starting number state.
export function crc32Init(): number {
    return 0xFFFFFFFF;
}

// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
//
// state: running number state (from init or a prior update).
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the updated number state (not yet finalized).
//
// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
export function crc32Update(state: number, data: Uint8Array): number {
    let crc: number = state;
    const n = data.length;
    let i = 0;
    while (i + 8 <= n) {
        const b03 = data[i] | (data[i+1] << 8) | (data[i+2] << 16) | (data[i+3] << 24);
        const b47 = data[i+4] | (data[i+5] << 8) | (data[i+6] << 16) | (data[i+7] << 24);
        const xored = (crc ^ b03) >>> 0;
        crc = (
            crcglot_slice_crc32[7][ xored         & 0xFF]
          ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[6][(xored >>>  8) & 0xFF]
          ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[5][(xored >>> 16) & 0xFF]
          ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[4][(xored >>> 24) & 0xFF]
          ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[3][ b47          & 0xFF]
          ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[2][(b47   >>>  8) & 0xFF]
          ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[1][(b47   >>> 16) & 0xFF]
          ^ crcglot_slice_crc32[0][(b47   >>> 24) & 0xFF]
        ) >>> 0;
        i += 8;
    }
    while (i < n) {
        crc = (crcglot_slice_crc32[0][(crc ^ data[i]) & 0xFF] ^ (crc >>> 8)) >>> 0;
        i += 1;
    }
    return crc;
}

// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
//
// state: accumulated number state from update.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
//
// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
export function crc32Finalize(state: number): number {
    return (state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF) >>> 0;
}

// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
//
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
export function crc32(data: Uint8Array): number {
    return crc32Finalize(crc32Update(crc32Init(), data));
}

// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
//
// Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
//
// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
//
// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
export function crc32SelfTest(): boolean {
    if (crc32(new Uint8Array([])) !== 0x00000000) return false;
    if (crc32(new Uint8Array([0x31,0x32,0x33,0x34,0x35,0x36,0x37,0x38,0x39])) !== 0xCBF43926) return false;
    {
        let s = crc32Init();
        for (let i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
            s = crc32Update(s, new Uint8Array([i]));
        }
        if (crc32Finalize(s) !== 0x29058C73) return false;
    }
    {
        let s = crc32Init();
        for (let i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
            s = crc32Update(s, new Uint8Array([(i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF]));
        }
        if (crc32Finalize(s) !== 0x6D4552DB) return false;
    }
    return true;
}
```

</details>

<a id="example-verilog-bitwise"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### Verilog — bit-by-bit

</summary>

```bash
crcglot verilog crc32
```

```systemverilog
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     state = crc32_init();
//     state = crc32_update(state, byte_in);  // call once per byte
//     crc = crc32_finalize(state);
//
// One-shot: crc32(data)
// Verify:   crc32_self_test returns 1'b1 on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// update consumes ONE byte per call -- the one-shot wrapper loops over the array for you.
//
// Simulator reference (verified under ghdl / iverilog), not a drop-in synthesizable RTL core.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    verilog
//     variant:   bitwise
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    snake

`ifndef CRC32_PKG_SV
`define CRC32_PKG_SV

package crc32_pkg;

    // Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
    //
    // Returns the starting 32-bit state.
    function automatic [31:0] crc32_init();
        crc32_init = 32'hFFFFFFFF;
    endfunction

    // Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
    //
    // state: running 32-bit state (from init or a prior update).
    // byte_in: a single input byte (8 bits).
    //
    // Returns the updated 32-bit state (not yet finalized).
    //
    // Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    //
    // Consumes one byte per call -- loop over your message bytes.
    function automatic [31:0] crc32_update(input [31:0] state, input [7:0] byte_in);
        logic [31:0] crc;
        crc = state;
        crc = crc ^ {{24{1'b0}}, byte_in};
        for (int j = 0; j < 8; j++) begin
            if (crc[0] == 1'b1) begin
                crc = (crc >> 1) ^ 32'hEDB88320;
            end else begin
                crc = crc >> 1;
            end
        end
        crc32_update = crc;
    endfunction

    // Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
    //
    // state: accumulated 32-bit state from update.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    function automatic [31:0] crc32_finalize(input [31:0] state);
        logic [31:0] crc;
        crc = state;
        crc32_finalize = crc ^ 32'hFFFFFFFF;
    endfunction

    // One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
    //
    // data: the packed message as a byte-unsigned array.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    function automatic [31:0] crc32(input byte unsigned data[]);
        logic [31:0] s;
        s = crc32_init();
        foreach (data[i]) begin
            s = crc32_update(s, data[i]);
        end
        crc32 = crc32_finalize(s);
    endfunction

    // Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
    //
    // Returns 1'b1 iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
    //
    // Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
    //
    // Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    function automatic bit crc32_self_test();
        byte unsigned data[] = '{
            8'h31, 8'h32, 8'h33, 8'h34, 8'h35,
            8'h36, 8'h37, 8'h38, 8'h39
        };
        return (crc32(data) == 32'hCBF43926);
    endfunction

endpackage

`endif
```

</details>

<a id="example-vhdl-bitwise"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### VHDL — bit-by-bit

</summary>

```bash
crcglot vhdl crc32
```

```vhdl
-- crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
-- Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
-- check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
--
-- Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
-- number of times over successive chunks of the message:
--
--     s := crc32_init();
--     s := crc32_update(s, chunk);  -- chunk length a multiple of 8
--     crc := crc32_finalize(s);
--
-- One-shot: crc32(data)
-- Verify:   crc32_self_test returns true on success; run it once on your
--           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
--
-- Input vectors are packed bytes; the length must be a multiple of 8 bits.
--
-- Simulator reference (verified under ghdl), not a drop-in synthesizable RTL core.
--
-- Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
-- Reproduce with crcglot:
--     version:   0.22.0
--     algorithm: crc32
--     target:    vhdl
--     variant:   bitwise
--     comment:   plain
--     symbol:    crc32
--     naming:    snake

library ieee;
use ieee.std_logic_1164.all;
use ieee.numeric_std.all;

package crc32_pkg is

    -- Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
    --
    -- Returns the starting 32-bit std_logic_vector state.
    function crc32_init return std_logic_vector;

    -- Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
    --
    -- state: running 32-bit std_logic_vector state (from init or a prior update).
    -- data: the message as a packed std_logic_vector (length a multiple of 8).
    --
    -- Returns the updated 32-bit std_logic_vector state (not yet finalized).
    --
    -- Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    function crc32_update(state: std_logic_vector; data: std_logic_vector) return std_logic_vector;

    -- Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
    --
    -- state: accumulated 32-bit std_logic_vector state from update.
    --
    -- Returns the finished CRC value.
    --
    -- Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    function crc32_finalize(state: std_logic_vector) return std_logic_vector;

    -- One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
    --
    -- data: the message as a packed std_logic_vector (length a multiple of 8).
    --
    -- Returns the finished CRC value.
    function crc32(data: std_logic_vector) return std_logic_vector;

    -- Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
    --
    -- Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
    --
    -- Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
    --
    -- Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    function crc32_self_test return boolean;
end package;

package body crc32_pkg is

    function crc32_init return std_logic_vector is
        variable s: unsigned(31 downto 0) := x"FFFFFFFF";
    begin
        return std_logic_vector(s);
    end function;

    function crc32_update(state: std_logic_vector; data: std_logic_vector) return std_logic_vector is
        variable crc: unsigned(31 downto 0) := unsigned(state);
        variable byte: unsigned(7 downto 0);
        -- Normalize indexing regardless of caller's slice direction.
        constant d: std_logic_vector(data'length - 1 downto 0) := data;
        constant n: natural := data'length / 8;
    begin
        for i in 0 to n - 1 loop
            byte := unsigned(d((n - i)*8 - 1 downto (n - i - 1)*8));
            crc := crc xor resize(byte, 32);
            for j in 0 to 7 loop
                if crc(0) = '1' then
                    crc := shift_right(crc, 1) xor x"EDB88320";
                else
                    crc := shift_right(crc, 1);
                end if;
            end loop;
        end loop;
        return std_logic_vector(crc);
    end function;

    function crc32_finalize(state: std_logic_vector) return std_logic_vector is
        variable crc: unsigned(31 downto 0) := unsigned(state);
    begin
        return std_logic_vector(crc xor x"FFFFFFFF");
    end function;

    function crc32(data: std_logic_vector) return std_logic_vector is
    begin
        return crc32_finalize(crc32_update(crc32_init, data));
    end function;

    -- Run the canonical reveng check value; returns true on success.
    function crc32_self_test return boolean is
        constant kCheckInput: std_logic_vector(71 downto 0) :=
            x"313233343536373839";  -- ASCII "123456789"
    begin
        return unsigned(crc32(kCheckInput)) = x"CBF43926";
    end function;
end package body;
```

</details>

## Comment styles

The `--comment` flag picks the documentation style of the generated code; the algorithm and inner loop are identical.  Each block below is `crc32` (bit-by-bit) in one style, so you can match the convention your codebase already uses (Doxygen, JavaDoc, rustdoc, Google/NumPy/reST docstrings, ...).  `plain` -- professional comments in the language's native syntax -- is the default and is shown alongside each language's specialized styles for comparison.  Verilog and VHDL support only `plain` and are omitted here.

- **C / C++**: [Plain](#style-c-plain) · [Doxygen](#style-c-doxygen)
- **C#**: [Plain](#style-csharp-plain) · [Doxygen](#style-csharp-doxygen) · [DocFX](#style-csharp-docfx)
- **Go**: [Plain](#style-go-plain) · [Godoc](#style-go-godoc)
- **Java**: [Plain](#style-java-plain) · [Doxygen](#style-java-doxygen) · [Javadoc](#style-java-javadoc)
- **Python**: [Plain](#style-python-plain) · [Google](#style-python-google) · [NumPy](#style-python-numpy) · [reStructuredText](#style-python-rest)
- **Rust**: [Plain](#style-rust-plain) · [Rustdoc](#style-rust-rustdoc)
- **TypeScript**: [Plain](#style-typescript-plain) · [JSDoc](#style-typescript-jsdoc)

<a id="style-c-plain"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### C / C++ — Plain

</summary>

_Human-readable comments in the language's native syntax_

```bash
crcglot c crc32 --comment plain
```

**Header (`.h`)**

```c
/* crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
 * Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
 * check: crc32(data, len) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
 *
 * Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
 * number of times over successive chunks of the message:
 *
 *     uint32_t s = crc32_init();
 *     s = crc32_update(s, chunk, chunk_len);
 *     uint32_t crc = crc32_finalize(s);
 *
 * One-shot: crc32(data, len)
 * Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns 0 on success; run it once on your
 *           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
 *
 * Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
 * Reproduce with crcglot:
 *     version:   0.22.0
 *     algorithm: crc32
 *     target:    c
 *     variant:   bitwise
 *     comment:   plain
 *     symbol:    crc32
 *     naming:    snake
 */
#ifndef CRC32_H
#define CRC32_H

#include <stdint.h>
#include <stddef.h>

#ifdef __cplusplus
extern "C" {
#endif

/* Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
 *
 * Returns the starting uint32_t state.
 */
uint32_t crc32_init(void);

/* Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
 *
 * state: running uint32_t state (from init or a prior update).
 * data: pointer to the message bytes.
 * len: number of bytes available at data.
 *
 * Returns the updated uint32_t state (not yet finalized).
 *
 * Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
 */
uint32_t crc32_update(uint32_t state, const uint8_t *data, size_t len);

/* Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
 *
 * state: accumulated uint32_t state from update.
 *
 * Returns the finished CRC value.
 *
 * Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
 */
uint32_t crc32_finalize(uint32_t state);

/* One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
 *
 * data: pointer to the message bytes.
 * len: number of bytes available at data.
 *
 * Returns the finished CRC value.
 */
uint32_t crc32(const uint8_t *data, size_t len);

/* Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
 *
 * Returns 0 iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
 *
 * Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
 *
 * Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
 */
int crc32_self_test(void);

#ifndef CRCGLOT_NO_PROVENANCE
#ifndef CRCGLOT_PROVENANCE_T_DEFINED
#define CRCGLOT_PROVENANCE_T_DEFINED
typedef struct {
    const char *version;
    const char *algorithm;
    const char *target;
    const char *variant;
    const char *comment;
    const char *symbol;
    const char *naming;
} crcglot_provenance_t;
#endif
extern const crcglot_provenance_t crc32_provenance;
#endif

#ifdef __cplusplus
}
#endif

#endif /* CRC32_H */
```

**Source (`.c`)**

```c
/* crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
 * Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
 * check: crc32(data, len) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
 *
 * Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
 * number of times over successive chunks of the message:
 *
 *     uint32_t s = crc32_init();
 *     s = crc32_update(s, chunk, chunk_len);
 *     uint32_t crc = crc32_finalize(s);
 *
 * One-shot: crc32(data, len)
 * Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns 0 on success; run it once on your
 *           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
 *
 * Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
 * Reproduce with crcglot:
 *     version:   0.22.0
 *     algorithm: crc32
 *     target:    c
 *     variant:   bitwise
 *     comment:   plain
 *     symbol:    crc32
 *     naming:    snake
 */
#include "crc32.h"

uint32_t crc32_init(void) {
    return 0xFFFFFFFFU;
}

uint32_t crc32_update(uint32_t state, const uint8_t *data, size_t len) {
    uint32_t crc = state;
    for (size_t i = 0; i < len; i++) {
        crc ^= data[i];
        for (int j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            if ((crc & 1U) != 0U) {
                crc = (crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320U;
            } else {
                crc >>= 1;
            }
        }
    }
    return crc;
}

uint32_t crc32_finalize(uint32_t state) {
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFFU;
}

uint32_t crc32(const uint8_t *data, size_t len) {
    return crc32_finalize(crc32_update(crc32_init(), data, len));
}

int crc32_self_test(void) {
    static const uint8_t kCheckInput[] = "123456789";
    int failed = 0;
    if (crc32(kCheckInput, 0) != 0x00000000U) {
        failed = 1;
    }
    if (crc32(kCheckInput, 9) != 0xCBF43926U) {
        failed = 1;
    }
    {
        uint32_t s = crc32_init();
        for (unsigned int i = 0U; i < 256U; i++) {
            uint8_t b = (uint8_t)i;
            s = crc32_update(s, &b, 1);
        }
        if (crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73U) {
            failed = 1;
        }
    }
    {
        uint32_t s = crc32_init();
        for (unsigned int i = 0U; i < 1024U; i++) {
            uint8_t b = (uint8_t)(((i * 167U) + 13U) & 0xFFU);
            s = crc32_update(s, &b, 1);
        }
        if (crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DBU) {
            failed = 1;
        }
    }
    return (failed != 0) ? 1 : 0;
}

#ifndef CRCGLOT_NO_PROVENANCE
const crcglot_provenance_t crc32_provenance = {
    .version   = "0.22.0",
    .algorithm = "crc32",
    .target    = "c",
    .variant   = "bitwise",
    .comment   = "plain",
    .symbol    = "crc32",
    .naming    = "snake",
};
#endif
```

</details>

```c
/** @file
 * @brief crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
 *
 * Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.

 *     s = crc32_update(s, chunk, chunk_len);
```

**Source (`.c`)**

```c
/** @file
 * @brief crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
 *
 * Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
 * check: crc32(data, len) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
 *
 * Streaming -- call init, then update over each chunk, then finalize:
 * @code
 *     uint32_t s = crc32_init();
 *     s = crc32_update(s, chunk, chunk_len);
 *     uint32_t crc = crc32_finalize(s);
 * @endcode
 *
 * One-shot: crc32(data, len)
 * @note Verify with crc32_self_test() (returns 0 on success); run it once on your toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
 *
 * @note Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
 * Reproduce with crcglot:
 *     version:   0.22.0
 *     algorithm: crc32
 *     target:    c
 *     variant:   bitwise
 *     comment:   doxygen
 *     symbol:    crc32
 *     naming:    snake
 */
#include "crc32.h"

uint32_t crc32_init(void) {
    return 0xFFFFFFFFU;
}

uint32_t crc32_update(uint32_t state, const uint8_t *data, size_t len) {
    uint32_t crc = state;
    for (size_t i = 0; i < len; i++) {
        crc ^= data[i];
        for (int j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            if ((crc & 1U) != 0U) {
                crc = (crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320U;
            } else {
                crc >>= 1;
            }
        }
    }
    return crc;
}

uint32_t crc32_finalize(uint32_t state) {
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFFU;
}

uint32_t crc32(const uint8_t *data, size_t len) {
    return crc32_finalize(crc32_update(crc32_init(), data, len));
}

int crc32_self_test(void) {
    static const uint8_t kCheckInput[] = "123456789";
    int failed = 0;
    if (crc32(kCheckInput, 0) != 0x00000000U) {
        failed = 1;
    }
    if (crc32(kCheckInput, 9) != 0xCBF43926U) {
        failed = 1;
    }
    {
        uint32_t s = crc32_init();
        for (unsigned int i = 0U; i < 256U; i++) {
            uint8_t b = (uint8_t)i;
            s = crc32_update(s, &b, 1);
        }
        if (crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73U) {
            failed = 1;
        }
    }
    {
        uint32_t s = crc32_init();
        for (unsigned int i = 0U; i < 1024U; i++) {
            uint8_t b = (uint8_t)(((i * 167U) + 13U) & 0xFFU);
            s = crc32_update(s, &b, 1);
        }
        if (crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DBU) {
            failed = 1;
        }
    }
    return (failed != 0) ? 1 : 0;
}

#ifndef CRCGLOT_NO_PROVENANCE
const crcglot_provenance_t crc32_provenance = {
    .version   = "0.22.0",
    .algorithm = "crc32",
    .target    = "c",
    .variant   = "bitwise",
    .comment   = "doxygen",
    .symbol    = "crc32",
    .naming    = "snake",
};
#endif
```

<a id="style-csharp-plain"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### C# — Plain

</summary>

_Human-readable comments in the language's native syntax_

```bash
crcglot csharp crc32 --comment plain
```

```csharp
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: Crc32.Crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     uint s = Crc32.Crc32Init();
//     s = Crc32.Crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
//     uint crc = Crc32.Crc32Finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: Crc32.Crc32(data)
// Verify:   Crc32.Crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    csharp
//     variant:   bitwise
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    pascal

using System;

public static class Crc32
{
    // Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
    //
    // Returns the starting uint state.
    public static uint Crc32Init() {
        return 0xFFFFFFFFu;
    }

    // Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
    //
    // state: running uint state (from init or a prior update).
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the updated uint state (not yet finalized).
    //
    // Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    public static uint Crc32Update(uint state, byte[] data) {
        uint crc = state;
        foreach (byte b in data) {
            crc ^= b;
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
                if ((crc & 0x00000001u) != 0)
                    crc = (uint)((crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320u);
                else
                    crc >>= 1;
            }
        }
        return crc;
    }

    // Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
    //
    // state: accumulated uint state from update.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    public static uint Crc32Finalize(uint state) {
        return (uint)(state ^ 0xFFFFFFFFu);
    }

    // One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
    //
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    public static uint Crc32(byte[] data) {
        return Crc32Finalize(Crc32Update(Crc32Init(), data));
    }

    // Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
    //
    // Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
    //
    // Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
    //
    // Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    public static bool Crc32SelfTest() {
        if (Crc32(new byte[0]) != 0x00000000u) return false;
        if (Crc32(new byte[] { 0x31, 0x32, 0x33, 0x34, 0x35, 0x36, 0x37, 0x38, 0x39 }) != 0xCBF43926u) return false;
        {
            uint s = Crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
                s = Crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte)i });
            }
            if (Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73u) return false;
        }
        {
            uint s = Crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
                s = Crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte)((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) });
            }
            if (Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DBu) return false;
        }
        return true;
    }
}
```

</details>

<a id="style-csharp-doxygen"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### C# — Doxygen

</summary>

_Doxygen /** @brief @param @return */ markup_

```bash

```

```csharp
/** @file
 * @brief crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
 *
 * Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
 * check: Crc32.Crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
 *
 * Streaming -- call init, then update over each chunk, then finalize:
 * @code
 *     uint s = Crc32.Crc32Init();
 *     s = Crc32.Crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
 *     uint crc = Crc32.Crc32Finalize(s);
 * @endcode
 *
 * One-shot: Crc32.Crc32(data)
 * @note Verify with Crc32.Crc32SelfTest() (returns true on success); run it once on your toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
 *
 * @note Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
 * Reproduce with crcglot:
 *     version:   0.22.0
 *     algorithm: crc32
 *     target:    csharp
 *     variant:   bitwise
 *     comment:   doxygen
 *     symbol:    crc32
 *     naming:    pascal
 */

using System;

public static class Crc32
{
    /** @brief Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
     * @return the starting uint state.
     */
    public static uint Crc32Init() {
        return 0xFFFFFFFFu;
    }

    /** @brief Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
     *
     * @param state running uint state (from init or a prior update).
     * @param data the message bytes.
     * @return the updated uint state (not yet finalized).
     * @note Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
     */
    public static uint Crc32Update(uint state, byte[] data) {
        uint crc = state;
        foreach (byte b in data) {
            crc ^= b;
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
                if ((crc & 0x00000001u) != 0)
                    crc = (uint)((crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320u);
                else
                    crc >>= 1;
            }
        }
        return crc;
    }

    /** @brief Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
     *
     * @param state accumulated uint state from update.
     * @return the finished CRC value.
     * @note Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
     */
    public static uint Crc32Finalize(uint state) {
        return (uint)(state ^ 0xFFFFFFFFu);
    }

    /** @brief One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
     *
     * @param data the message bytes.
     * @return the finished CRC value.
     */
    public static uint Crc32(byte[] data) {
        return Crc32Finalize(Crc32Update(Crc32Init(), data));
    }

    /** @brief Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
     * @return true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
     * @note Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
     * @note Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
     */
    public static bool Crc32SelfTest() {
        if (Crc32(new byte[0]) != 0x00000000u) return false;
        if (Crc32(new byte[] { 0x31, 0x32, 0x33, 0x34, 0x35, 0x36, 0x37, 0x38, 0x39 }) != 0xCBF43926u) return false;
        {
            uint s = Crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
                s = Crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte)i });
            }
            if (Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73u) return false;
        }
        {
            uint s = Crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
                s = Crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte)((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) });
            }
            if (Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DBu) return false;
        }
        return true;
    }
}
```

</details>

<a id="style-csharp-docfx"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### C# — DocFX

</summary>

_C# XML doc comments (/// <summary> <param> <returns>)_

```bash
crcglot csharp crc32 --comment docfx
```

```csharp
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: Crc32.Crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     uint s = Crc32.Crc32Init();
//     s = Crc32.Crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
//     uint crc = Crc32.Crc32Finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: Crc32.Crc32(data)
// Verify:   Crc32.Crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    csharp
//     variant:   bitwise
//     comment:   docfx
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    pascal

using System;

public static class Crc32
{
    /// <summary>
    /// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
    /// </summary>
    /// <returns>the starting uint state.</returns>
    public static uint Crc32Init() {
        return 0xFFFFFFFFu;
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="state">running uint state (from init or a prior update).</param>
    /// <param name="data">the message bytes.</param>
    /// <returns>the updated uint state (not yet finalized).</returns>
    /// <remarks>
    /// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    /// </remarks>
    public static uint Crc32Update(uint state, byte[] data) {
        uint crc = state;
        foreach (byte b in data) {
            crc ^= b;
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
                if ((crc & 0x00000001u) != 0)
                    crc = (uint)((crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320u);
                else
                    crc >>= 1;
            }
        }
        return crc;
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="state">accumulated uint state from update.</param>
    /// <returns>the finished CRC value.</returns>
    /// <remarks>
    /// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    /// </remarks>
    public static uint Crc32Finalize(uint state) {
        return (uint)(state ^ 0xFFFFFFFFu);
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
    /// </summary>
    /// <param name="data">the message bytes.</param>
    /// <returns>the finished CRC value.</returns>
    public static uint Crc32(byte[] data) {
        return Crc32Finalize(Crc32Update(Crc32Init(), data));
    }

    /// <summary>
    /// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
    /// </summary>
    /// <returns>true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.</returns>
    /// <remarks>
    /// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
    /// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    /// </remarks>
    public static bool Crc32SelfTest() {
        if (Crc32(new byte[0]) != 0x00000000u) return false;
        if (Crc32(new byte[] { 0x31, 0x32, 0x33, 0x34, 0x35, 0x36, 0x37, 0x38, 0x39 }) != 0xCBF43926u) return false;
        {
            uint s = Crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
                s = Crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte)i });
            }
            if (Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73u) return false;
        }
        {
            uint s = Crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
                s = Crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte)((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) });
            }
            if (Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DBu) return false;
        }
        return true;
    }
}
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>

### Go — Plain

</summary>

_Human-readable comments in the language's native syntax_

```bash
crcglot go crc32 --comment plain
```

```go
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: Crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     s := Crc32Init()
//     s = Crc32Update(s, chunk)  // over each chunk of the message
//     crc := Crc32Finalize(s)
//
// One-shot: Crc32(data)
// Verify:   Crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    go
//     variant:   bitwise
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    pascal

package crc

// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
//
// Returns the starting uint32 state.
func Crc32Init() uint32 {
    return 0xFFFFFFFF
}

// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
//
// state: running uint32 state (from init or a prior update).
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the updated uint32 state (not yet finalized).
//
// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
func Crc32Update(state uint32, data []byte) uint32 {
    crc := state
    for _, b := range data {
        crc ^= uint32(b)
        for i := 0; i < 8; i++ {
            if crc&1 != 0 {
                crc = (crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320
            } else {
                crc >>= 1
            }
        }
    }
    return crc
}

// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
//
// state: accumulated uint32 state from update.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
//
// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
func Crc32Finalize(state uint32) uint32 {
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF
}

// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
//
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
func Crc32(data []byte) uint32 {
    return Crc32Finalize(Crc32Update(Crc32Init(), data))
}

// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
//
// Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
//
// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
//
// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
func Crc32SelfTest() bool {
    if Crc32([]byte("")) != 0x00000000 {
        return false
    }
    if Crc32([]byte("123456789")) != 0xCBF43926 {
        return false
    }
    s := Crc32Init()
    for i := 0; i < 256; i++ {
        s = Crc32Update(s, []byte{byte(i)})
    }
    if Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73 {
        return false
    }
    s = Crc32Init()
    for i := 0; i < 1024; i++ {
        s = Crc32Update(s, []byte{byte((i*167 + 13) & 0xFF)})
    }
    if Crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB {
        return false
    }
    return true
}
```

</details>

```java
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: CrcGlot.crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926

// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//

//     s = CrcGlot.crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
//     int crc = CrcGlot.crc32Finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: CrcGlot.crc32(data)
// Verify:   CrcGlot.crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    java
//     variant:   bitwise
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    camel

    //
    // Returns the starting int state.
    public static int crc32Init() {
        return 0xFFFFFFFF;
    }

    // Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
    //
    // state: running int state (from init or a prior update).
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the updated int state (not yet finalized).
    //
    // Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    public static int crc32Update(int state, byte[] data) {
        int crc = state;
        for (byte b : data) {
            crc ^= (b & 0xFF);
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
                if ((crc & 1) != 0)
                    crc = (crc >>> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320;
                else
                    crc >>>= 1;
            }
        }
        return crc;
    }

    // Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
    //
    // state: accumulated int state from update.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    //
    // width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
    public static int crc32Finalize(int state) {
        return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF;
    }

    // One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
    //
    // data: the message bytes.
    //
    // Returns the finished CRC value.
    //
    // width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
    public static int crc32(byte[] data) {
        return crc32Finalize(crc32Update(crc32Init(), data));
    }

    // Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
    //
    // Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
    //
    // Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.

    public static boolean crc32SelfTest() {
```

```java
/** @file
 * @brief crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
 *
 * Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
 * check: CrcGlot.crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
 *
 * Streaming -- call init, then update over each chunk, then finalize:
 * @code
 *     int s = CrcGlot.crc32Init();
 *     s = CrcGlot.crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
 *     int crc = CrcGlot.crc32Finalize(s);
 * @endcode
 *
 * One-shot: CrcGlot.crc32(data)
 * @note Verify with CrcGlot.crc32SelfTest() (returns true on success); run it once on your toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
 *
 * @note width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
 *
 * @note Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
 * Reproduce with crcglot:
 *     version:   0.22.0
 *     algorithm: crc32
 *     target:    java
 *     variant:   bitwise
 *     comment:   doxygen
 *     symbol:    crc32
 *     naming:    camel
 */

public final class CrcGlot {
    /** @brief Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
     * @return the starting int state.
     */
    public static int crc32Init() {
        return 0xFFFFFFFF;
    }

    /** @brief Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
     *
     * @param state running int state (from init or a prior update).
     * @param data the message bytes.
     * @return the updated int state (not yet finalized).
     * @note Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
     */
    public static int crc32Update(int state, byte[] data) {
        int crc = state;
        for (byte b : data) {
            crc ^= (b & 0xFF);
            for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
                if ((crc & 1) != 0)
                    crc = (crc >>> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320;
                else
                    crc >>>= 1;

        }
        return crc;
    }

    /** @brief Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
     *
     * @param state accumulated int state from update.
     * @return the finished CRC value.

     * @note width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
     */

        return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF;
    }

    /** @brief One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
     *
     * @param data the message bytes.
     * @return the finished CRC value.
     * @note width-32 results are a signed int bit pattern (negative when the high bit is set); call Integer.toUnsignedLong(x) for a 0..2^32-1 value.
     */
    public static int crc32(byte[] data) {
        return crc32Finalize(crc32Update(crc32Init(), data));
    }

    /** @brief Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
     * @return true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
     * @note Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
     * @note Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
     */
    public static boolean crc32SelfTest() {
        if (crc32(new byte[0]) != 0x00000000) return false;

        {

                s = crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte) i });
            }

                s = crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte) ((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) });

            if (crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB) return false;

        return true;
    }
}
```

```java
     * @return the finished CRC value.
     */
    public static int crc32(byte[] data) {
        return crc32Finalize(crc32Update(crc32Init(), data));
    }

    /** Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
     *
     * Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
     *
     * Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
     * @return true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
     */
    public static boolean crc32SelfTest() {
        if (crc32(new byte[0]) != 0x00000000) return false;
        if (crc32(new byte[] { 0x31, 0x32, 0x33, 0x34, 0x35, 0x36, 0x37, 0x38, 0x39 }) != 0xCBF43926) return false;
        {
            int s = crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
                s = crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte) i });
            }
            if (crc32Finalize(s) != 0x29058C73) return false;
        }
        {
            int s = crc32Init();
            for (int i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
                s = crc32Update(s, new byte[] { (byte) ((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) });
            }
            if (crc32Finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB) return false;
        }
        return true;
    }
}
```

</details>

<a id="style-python-plain"></a>

<details>
<summary>

### Python — Plain

</summary>

_Human-readable comments in the language's native syntax_

```bash
crcglot python crc32 --comment plain
```

```python
"""crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926

Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
number of times over successive chunks of the message:

    s = crc32_init()
    s = crc32_update(s, chunk)  # over each chunk of the message
    crc = crc32_finalize(s)

One-shot: crc32(data)
Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns True on success; run it once on your
          toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.

Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
Reproduce with crcglot:
    version:   0.22.0
    algorithm: crc32
    target:    python
    variant:   bitwise
    comment:   plain
    symbol:    crc32
    naming:    snake
"""


def crc32_init() -> int:
    """Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.

    Returns the starting int state.
    """
    return 0xFFFFFFFF


def crc32_update(state: int, data: bytes) -> int:
    """Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.

    state: running int state (from init or a prior update).
    data: the message bytes (a bytes-like object).

    Returns the updated int state (not yet finalized).

    Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
    """
    crc = state
    for byte in data:
        crc ^= byte
        for _ in range(8):
            if crc & 1:
                crc = (crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320
            else:
                crc >>= 1
    return crc


def crc32_finalize(state: int) -> int:
    """Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.

    state: accumulated int state from update.

    Returns the finished CRC value.

    Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    """
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF


def crc32(data: bytes) -> int:
    """One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.

    data: the message bytes (a bytes-like object).

    Returns the finished CRC value.
    """
    state = crc32_init()
    state = crc32_update(state, data)
    return crc32_finalize(state)


def crc32_self_test() -> bool:
    """Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.

    Returns True iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.

    Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.

    Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    """
    if crc32(b"") != 0x00000000:
        return False
    if crc32(b"123456789") != 0xCBF43926:
        return False
    s = crc32_init()
    for i in range(256):
        s = crc32_update(s, bytes([i]))
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73:
        return False
    s = crc32_init()
    for i in range(1024):
        s = crc32_update(s, bytes([(i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF]))
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB:
        return False
    return True
```

</details>

```python
"""crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG

Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926

Example:
    Streaming -- call init, then update over each chunk, then finalize::

        s = crc32_init()
        s = crc32_update(s, chunk)  # over each chunk of the message
        crc = crc32_finalize(s)

    One-shot: crc32(data)

Note:
    Verify with crc32_self_test() (returns True on success); run it once on your interpreter to catch a build / width mismatch.
    Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
    Reproduce with crcglot:
        version:   0.22.0
        algorithm: crc32
        target:    python
        variant:   bitwise
        comment:   google
        symbol:    crc32
        naming:    snake
"""


def crc32_init() -> int:
    """Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.

    Returns:
        the starting int state.
    """
    return 0xFFFFFFFF


def crc32_update(state: int, data: bytes) -> int:
    """Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.

    Args:
        state: running int state (from init or a prior update).
        data: the message bytes (a bytes-like object).

    Returns:
        the updated int state (not yet finalized).

    Note:
        Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.

                crc = (crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320
            else:
                crc >>= 1
    return crc

    Args:
        state: accumulated int state from update.

    Returns:
        the finished CRC value.

    Note:
        Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
    """
    return state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF


def crc32(data: bytes) -> int:
    """One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.

    Args:
        data: the message bytes (a bytes-like object).

    Returns:
        the finished CRC value.
    """

    state = crc32_update(state, data)
    return crc32_finalize(state)

    """Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.

    Returns:
        True iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.

    Note:
        Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
        Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
    """
    if crc32(b"") != 0x00000000:
        return False
    if crc32(b"123456789") != 0xCBF43926:
        return False
    s = crc32_init()
    for i in range(256):
        s = crc32_update(s, bytes([i]))
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73:
        return False
    s = crc32_init()
    for i in range(1024):
        s = crc32_update(s, bytes([(i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF]))
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB:
        return False
    return True
```

### Rust — Plain

</summary>

_Human-readable comments in the language's native syntax_

```bash
crcglot rust crc32 --comment plain
```

```rust
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
//
// Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
// number of times over successive chunks of the message:
//
//     let s = crc32_init();
//     let s = crc32_update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk
//     let crc = crc32_finalize(s);
//
// One-shot: crc32(data)
// Verify:   crc32_self_test() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    rust
//     variant:   bitwise
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    snake

/// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
///
/// Returns the starting u32 state.
pub fn crc32_init() -> u32 {
    0xFFFFFFFF
}

/// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
///
/// state: running u32 state (from init or a prior update).
/// data: the message bytes.
///
/// Returns the updated u32 state (not yet finalized).
///
/// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
pub fn crc32_update(state: u32, data: &[u8]) -> u32 {
    let mut crc: u32 = state;
    for &byte in data {
        crc ^= byte as u32;
        for _ in 0..8 {
            if crc & 1 != 0 {
                crc = (crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320;
            } else {
                crc >>= 1;
            }
        }
    }
    crc
}

/// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
///
/// state: accumulated u32 state from update.
///
/// Returns the finished CRC value.
///
/// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
pub fn crc32_finalize(state: u32) -> u32 {
    state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF
}

/// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
///
/// data: the message bytes.
///
/// Returns the finished CRC value.
pub fn crc32(data: &[u8]) -> u32 {
    crc32_finalize(crc32_update(crc32_init(), data))
}

/// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
///
/// Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
///
/// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
///
/// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
pub fn crc32_self_test() -> bool {
    if crc32(b"") != 0x00000000_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    if crc32(b"123456789") != 0xCBF43926_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    let mut s = crc32_init();
    for i in 0u32..256 {
        s = crc32_update(s, &[i as u8]);
    }
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x29058C73_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    s = crc32_init();
    for i in 0u32..1024 {
        s = crc32_update(s, &[((i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF) as u8]);
    }
    if crc32_finalize(s) != 0x6D4552DB_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    true
}
```

```rust
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.

    0xFFFFFFFF
}

///

/// * `state` - running u32 state (from init or a prior update).
/// * `data` - the message bytes.
///
/// # Returns
///
/// The updated u32 state (not yet finalized).
///
/// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.

        crc ^= byte as u32;
        for _ in 0..8 {
            if crc & 1 != 0 {
                crc = (crc >> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320;
            } else {
                crc >>= 1;
            }
        }
    }
    crc
}

/// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
///
/// # Arguments
///
/// * `state` - accumulated u32 state from update.
///
/// # Returns
///
/// The finished CRC value.
///
/// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
pub fn crc32_finalize(state: u32) -> u32 {
    state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF
}

/// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
///
/// # Arguments
///
/// * `data` - the message bytes.
///
/// # Returns
///
/// The finished CRC value.
pub fn crc32(data: &[u8]) -> u32 {

}

/// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
///
/// # Returns
///
/// True iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
///
/// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
///
/// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
pub fn crc32_self_test() -> bool {
    if crc32(b"") != 0x00000000_u32 {
        return false;
    }
    if crc32(b"123456789") != 0xCBF43926_u32 {
        return false;
```

```typescript
// crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
// Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
// check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926

//
// One-shot: crc32(data)
// Verify:   crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your
//           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
//
// Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
// Reproduce with crcglot:
//     version:   0.22.0
//     algorithm: crc32
//     target:    typescript
//     variant:   bitwise
//     comment:   plain
//     symbol:    crc32
//     naming:    camel

// Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
//
// Returns the starting number state.
export function crc32Init(): number {
    return 0xFFFFFFFF;
}

// Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
//
// state: running number state (from init or a prior update).
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the updated number state (not yet finalized).
//
// Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
export function crc32Update(state: number, data: Uint8Array): number {
    let crc: number = state;
    for (const byte of data) {
        crc ^= byte;
        for (let j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            if ((crc & 1) !== 0) {
                crc = (crc >>> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320;
            } else {
                crc >>>= 1;
            }
        }
    }
    return crc;
}

// Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
//
// state: accumulated number state from update.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
//
// Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
export function crc32Finalize(state: number): number {
    return (state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF) >>> 0;
}

// One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
//
// data: the message bytes.
//
// Returns the finished CRC value.
export function crc32(data: Uint8Array): number {
    return crc32Finalize(crc32Update(crc32Init(), data));
}

// Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
//
// Returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
//
// Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
//
// Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
export function crc32SelfTest(): boolean {
    if (crc32(new Uint8Array([])) !== 0x00000000) return false;
    if (crc32(new Uint8Array([0x31,0x32,0x33,0x34,0x35,0x36,0x37,0x38,0x39])) !== 0xCBF43926) return false;
    {
        let s = crc32Init();
        for (let i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
            s = crc32Update(s, new Uint8Array([i]));
        }
        if (crc32Finalize(s) !== 0x29058C73) return false;
    }
    {
        let s = crc32Init();
        for (let i = 0; i < 1024; i++) {
            s = crc32Update(s, new Uint8Array([(i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF]));
        }
        if (crc32Finalize(s) !== 0x6D4552DB) return false;
    }
    return true;
}
```

</details>

### TypeScript — JSDoc

_TSDoc /** @param x - ... @returns */ comments_

```bash
crcglot typescript crc32 --comment jsdoc
```

```typescript
/** crc32 -- ISO 3309, ITU-T V.42, Ethernet, PKZIP, PNG
 * Parameters: width=32, poly=0x04C11DB7, init=0xFFFFFFFF, refin=true, refout=true, xorout=0xFFFFFFFF.
 * check: crc32(data) over "123456789" == 0xCBF43926
 *
 * Streaming (init -> update -> finalize); update may be called any
 * number of times over successive chunks of the message:
 *
 *     let s = crc32Init();
 *     s = crc32Update(s, chunk);  // over each chunk of the message
 *     const crc = crc32Finalize(s);
 *
 * One-shot: crc32(data)
 * Verify:   crc32SelfTest() returns true on success; run it once on your
 *           toolchain to catch a compiler / endianness mismatch.
 *
 * Generated by crcglot from reveng/crc32 -- a verified reference implementation.
 * Reproduce with crcglot:
 *     version:   0.22.0
 *     algorithm: crc32
 *     target:    typescript
 *     variant:   bitwise
 *     comment:   jsdoc
 *     symbol:    crc32
 *     naming:    camel
 */

/** Return the initial CRC state to begin a computation.
 * @returns the starting number state.
 */
export function crc32Init(): number {
    return 0xFFFFFFFF;
}

/** Fold input into the running CRC state and return the new state.
 *
 * Call init -> update (any number of times) -> finalize.
 *
 * @param state - running number state (from init or a prior update).
 * @param data - the message bytes.
 * @returns the updated number state (not yet finalized).
 */

    for (const byte of data) {
        crc ^= byte;

            if ((crc & 1) !== 0) {
                crc = (crc >>> 1) ^ 0xEDB88320;
            } else {
                crc >>>= 1;
            }
        }
    }
    return crc;
}

/** Apply the final XOR to produce the CRC.
 *
 * Do not feed the finalized value back into update.
 *
 * @param state - accumulated number state from update.
 * @returns the finished CRC value.
 */
export function crc32Finalize(state: number): number {
    return (state ^ 0xFFFFFFFF) >>> 0;
}

/** One-shot convenience: init + a single update + finalize.
 *
 * @param data - the message bytes.
 * @returns the finished CRC value.
 */

}

/** Self-test the implementation against independent reference CRCs.
 *
 * Catalogue algorithms check four fixed inputs (the empty string, "123456789", all 256 byte values, and a 1 KiB pattern); the two large inputs are regenerated with a byte-at-a-time loop, so no big array is embedded.  The references come from two independent engines that had to agree.
 *
 * Run once on your target toolchain -- it is the cheapest way to catch a compiler / endianness / width mismatch before trusting the output.
 * @returns true iff the generated CRC reproduces every embedded reference value.
 */
export function crc32SelfTest(): boolean {
    if (crc32(new Uint8Array([])) !== 0x00000000) return false;
    if (crc32(new Uint8Array([0x31,0x32,0x33,0x34,0x35,0x36,0x37,0x38,0x39])) !== 0xCBF43926) return false;

            s = crc32Update(s, new Uint8Array([(i * 167 + 13) & 0xFF]));
```
